Roberts, Robert S. Laramee, Gary A. Smith, Paul Brookes, Tony D\u2019Cruze in IEEE Transactions on Visualization and Computer Graphics (IEEE TVCG), \n Volume 25, Issue 3, March 2019, pages 1575-1590\n\nhttps://doi.org/10.1109/TVCG.2018.2808969 \n\nAbstract:\nThe Parallel Coordinates plot is a popular tool for the visualization of high-dimensional data. One of the main challenges when\nusing parallel coordinates is occlusion and overplotting resulting from large data sets. Brushing is a popular approach to address these challenges. Since its conception, limited improvements have been made to brushing both in the form of visual design and functional interaction. We present a set of novel, smart brushing techniques that enhance the standard interactive brushing of a parallel coordinates plot. We introduce two new interaction concepts: Higher-order, sketch-based brushing, and smart, data-driven brushing. Higher-order brushes support interactive, flexible, n-dimensional pattern searches involving an arbitrary number of dimensions. Smart, data-driven brushing provides interactive, real-time guidance to the user during the brushing process based on derived meta-data. In addition, we implement a selection of novel enhancements and user options that complement the two techniques as well as enhance the exploration and analytical ability of the user. We demonstrate the utility and evaluate the results using a case study with a large, high-dimensional, real-world telecommunication data set and we report domain expert feedback from the data suppliers.\n\nPDF:\nhttp://cs.swan.ac.uk/~csbob/research/callCenter/brushing/roberts18smart.pdf", "tags": ["parallel coordinates", "brushing techniques", "information visualization", "visual analytics"], "defaultLanguage": "en", "title": "Smart Brushing for Parallel Coordinates", "channelId": "UCQly2ZxY-CHqwG7pO-xOy5Q"}, "contentDetails": {"duration": "PT9M34S"}, "statistics": {"viewCount": "187", "dislikeCount": "0", "likeCount": "6", "favoriteCount": "0", "commentCount": "0"}, "id": "ogfR4emjgP4"}], "idx_paper": "10.1109/TVCG.2018.2808969"}, {"q": "10.1109/TII.2018.2847736", "items": [{"snippet": {"channelTitle": "Alfredo N\u00fa\u00f1ez Vicencio", "publishedAt": "2016-10-20T10:41:51Z", "description": "In the framework of the H2020 NeTIRail-INFRA project, we have performed a measurement campaign in the track Bartolomeu-Zarnersti near Brasov in Romania. Shariq N. Iqbal et al (2019), PLOS Computational Biology https://doi.org/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1006895\n\nUnderstanding the principles by which agents interact with both complex environments and each other is a key goal of decision neuroscience. However, most previous studies have used experimental paradigms in which choices are discrete (and few), play is static, and optimal solutions are known.\n\nYet in natural environments, interactions between agents typically involve continuous action spaces, ongoing dynamics, and no known optimal solution. Here, we seek to bridge this divide by using a \u201cpenalty shot\u201d task in which pairs of monkeys competed against each other in a competitive, real-time video game.\n\nWe modeled monkeys\u2019 strategies as driven by stochastically evolving goals, onscreen positions that served as set points for a control model that produced observed joystick movements. We fit this goal-based dynamical system model using approximate Bayesian inference methods, using neural networks to parameterize players\u2019 goals as a dynamic mixture of Gaussian components.\n\nOur model is conceptually simple, constructed of interpretable components, and capable of generating synthetic data that capture the complexity of real player dynamics. We further characterized players\u2019 strategies using the number of change points on each trial.\n\nWe found that this complexity varied more across sessions than within sessions, and that more complex strategies benefited offensive players but not defensive players. Together, our experimental paradigm and model offer a powerful combination of tools for the study of realistic social dynamics in the laboratory setting.\n\nGood channel: https://www.youtube.com/Dlium\nSubscribe, like and comment.\n\nGood website: https://www.dlium.com\nBookmark, subscribe and comment.", "tags": ["PLOS Computational Biology", "Games", "Monkeys", "Neural networks", "Game theory", "Decision making", "Dynamical systems", "Simulation and modeling", "Rhesus monkeys"], "title": "Latent goal models for dynamic strategic interaction", "channelId": "UC32BboXfQ_tDCV8y1ttx7cg"}, "contentDetails": {"duration": "PT1M1S"}, "statistics": {"viewCount": "15", "dislikeCount": "0", "likeCount": "0", "favoriteCount": "0", "commentCount": "0"}, "id": "L1LoabMB4IQ"}], "idx_paper": "10.1371/journal.pcbi.1006895"}, {"q": "10.1177/0278364918796267", "items": [{"snippet": {"defaultAudioLanguage": "en", "channelTitle": "Omur Arslan", "publishedAt": "2018-11-15T09:24:21Z", "description": "Omur Arslan and Daniel E. Our algorithm introduces a novel use of separating hyperplanes for identifying the robot\u2019s local obstacle-free convex neighborhood, affording a reactive (online-computed) continuous and piecewise smooth closed-loop vector field whose smooth flow brings almost all configurations in the robot\u2019s free space to a designated goal location, with the guarantee of no collisions along the way. Within each group, the researchers are comparing gait, balance, lifting, sit-to-stand motion, and stair climbing before and after several types of treatments.\n\nThe biomechanical analysis can help determine if patients are using muscles efficiently after surgery and if their muscles are coordinated. The findings can be used to help fine tune physical therapy programs and help motivate patients to continue exercising. \n\nThe lab is the first spine-related human movement biomechanics lab to be incorporated within a private practice spine center in the United States. \n\nFor more info, you can visit: www.texasback.com\n\nYou can connect with Dr. Haddas at\nLinkedin: https://www.linkedin.com/in/rhaddas/\nResearch gate: https://www.researchgate.net/profile/Ram_Haddas\n\nHaddas R, Cox J, Belanger T, Boah AO, Ju KL, Derman PB. It has been approximated that about 15 million tons of surfactants are used a year according to Lara-Martin and others who did research on this subject in 2006. Some research done by K. Jardak and his colleges found that during the wastewater treatment process a lot of surfactants biodegrade due to oxidation during the one of the phases in the treatment process. The oxidation breaks down last carbon on the alkyl chain. The treatment process rids the wastewater of a majority of surfactants but not all, this is where the concern about the environmental effects comes from due to the fact that is a relatively small input into the environment but it is a consistent one.\n Jardak and his team also go into describing the two main types of surfactants anionic and nonionic surfactants. Anionic surfactants are the most common due to their cheap manufacturing cost and the ease at which they are absorbed into solids when in water. They cited one group of concern in the anionic surfactant class are perfluorooctanoic (PFO) which are used in shampoos and nonstick pans. PFO chemicals make are different than the ones in you dish soap due to the need for the protection against heat solubility in water. These types of surfactants are not biodegradable and need to be taken out in the water treatment process because they do bio accumulate like the heavy metal mercury. The reason for this state by Jardak is the bonds compared to the common anionic surfactant (alkylbenzene sulfonates) which has a carbon hydrogen bond PFOS have some fluorine carbon bonds which are a lot stronger. Nonionic surfactants are less common and are used usually in a mixture with other surfactants main for industrial use. On the contrary these nonionic surfactants have more restrictions because compared to anionic surfactants they do not break down well in the natural environment. Jardak further explains that when nonionic surfactants partially break down, they leave behind nonylphenol and octylphenol which are toxic to humans and aquatic life. Jardak and his team found that overall the effects of surfactants have physically on aquatic life create gill damage and decrease mobility of fish too decreased respiration and excess mucus build up along with causing skin irritation and sometimes allegories with humans. In other studies, Markowski and a group of scientists found that a presence of surfactants in water bodies can increase eutrophication because it inhibits oxygens ability to move deeper away from the surface. This causes more issues with dead zones forming and decreasing the area in which algae and fish can survive. On the cellular level surfactants cause depolarization of cells membrane causing decreased absorption and expulsion inhibiting the health of the organisms made clear by Jardak and his team.\n For mitigation purposes the most obvious answer is to swing away from using the surfactants that don\u2019t biodegrade vary easily and stick around in soil for centuries causing accumulation problems. We could also try and avoid and update cities waste disposal systems where untreated water does not enter water bodies along with improving wastewater treatment plants to improve the retention rate of surfactants in the waste sludge. \n\nSources: \nPalmer M, Hatley H. We studied the clinical course to explore appropriate treatment strategies. We retrospectively studied consecutive 33 patients who had CSC-HE. The disease stage was classified into 4 groups: group A, early head and neck cancer (HNC) and early esophageal cancer (EC); group B, early HNC and advanced EC; group C, advanced HNC and early EC; and group D, advanced HNC and advanced EC. As induction chemotherapy, the patients received 3 courses of TPF therapy (docetaxel 75mg/m 2 on day 1, cisplatin 75mg/m 2 on day 1, and 5-fluorouracil 750mg/m 2 on days 1-5) at 3-week intervals. The clinical courses and treatment outcomes were studied according to the disease stage of CSC-HE. The disease stage of CSC-HE was group A in 1 patient (3%), group B in 9 patients (27.3%), group C in 3 patients (9.1%), and group D in 20 patients (60.6%). The median follow-up was 26months, and the 2-year overall survival rate was 67.4%. In groups A, B, and C, the 2-year overall survival rate was 83.3%. In group D, the 2-year overall survival rate was 62.6%. Ten of 20 patients in group D received induction chemotherapy with TPF, and 6 patients were alive and disease free at the time of this writing. The treatment outcomes of patients with CSC-HE were relatively good. TPF induction chemotherapy might be an effective treatment for patients with advanced HNC and advanced EC. Copyright \u00a9 2018. \u7c21\u7a31LDL-cholesterol)\uff0c\u5373\u662f\u6703\u589e\u52a0\u60a3\u4e0a\u51a0\u5fc3\u75c5\u7684\u300c\u58de\u81bd\u56fa\u9187\u300d\uff0c\u98fd\u548c\u8102\u80aa\u542b\u91cf\u9ad8\u7684\u98df\u54c1\u5305\u62ec\u8089\u985e(\u725b\u3001\u8c6c\u3001\u7f8a\u3001\u96de\u7b49)\u3001\u6930\u5b50\u6cb9\u3001\u68d5\u6ada\u6cb9\u3001\u5976\u985e\u98df\u54c1(\u4f8b\u5982\u725b\u6cb9\u3001\u829d\u58eb\u3001\u5168\u8102\u5976\u7b49)\u3001\u8d77\u9165\u6cb9(shortening)\u7b49\uff0c\u9078\u7528\u7626\u8089\u3001\u4f4e\u8102\u5976\u985e\u98df\u54c1\u7b49\u80fd\u6e1b\u4f4e\u98f2\u98df\u4e2d\u98fd\u548c\u8102\u80aa\u7684\u4efd\u91cf\u3002\n\n(\u4e09)\u52a3\u8cea\u7684\u8102\u80aa \u2014 \u53cd\u5f0f\u8102\u80aa\uff1a\u5982\u540c\u98fd\u548c\u8102\u80aa\uff0c\u53cd\u5f0f\u8102\u80aa\u6703\u589e\u52a0\u4eba\u9ad4\u5167\u4f4e\u5bc6\u5ea6\u8102\u86cb\u767d\u81bd\u56fa\u9187(\u5373\u58de\u81bd\u56fa\u9187)\uff0c\u4f46\u8207\u98fd\u548c\u8102\u80aa\u4e0d\u540c\uff0c\u53cd\u5f0f\u8102\u80aa\u4ea6\u6703\u964d\u4f4e\u4eba\u9ad4\u5167\u9ad8\u5bc6\u5ea6\u8102\u86cb\u767d\u81bd\u56fa\u9187(high density lipoprotein cholesterol \u7c21\u7a31HDL-cholesterol\u5373\u597d\u81bd\u56fa\u9187)\uff0c\u5169\u8005\u90fd\u80fd\u589e\u52a0\u60a3\u4e0a\u51a0\u5fc3\u75c5\u7684\u98a8\u96aa\u3002\n\n\u53cd\u5f0f\u8102\u80aa\u662f\u5728\u5c07\u6db2\u9ad4\u8102\u80aa\u8f49\u70ba\u56fa\u9ad4\u8102\u80aa\u7684\u300c\u90e8\u4efd\u6c2b\u5316\u300d(partial hydrogenation)\u904e\u7a0b\u4e2d\u7522\u751f\uff0c\u4f7f\u7528\u53cd\u5f0f\u8102\u80aa\u4f7f\u98df\u7269\u8f03\u4e0d\u5bb9\u6613\u8150\u58de\uff0c\u4ee4\u552e\u8ce3\u7684\u98df\u54c1\u6709\u8f03\u9577\u7684\u8ca8\u67b6\u671f(shelf life\u5373\u5546\u54c1\u5132\u653e\u4e0d\u8b8a\u8cea\u7684\u671f\u9650)\u548c\u770b\u4f86\u53ca\u5403\u7684\u6642\u5019\u611f\u89ba\u8f03\u4e0d\u6cb9\u81a9\uff0c\u53cd\u5f0f\u8102\u80aa\u542b\u91cf\u9ad8\u7684\u98df\u7269\u5305\u62ec\u4eba\u9020\u725b\u6cb9\u3001\u714e\u70b8\u98df\u7269(\u4f8b\u5982\u85af\u7247\u3001\u70b8\u85af\u689d\u7b49)\u3001\u7cd5\u9905(\u5305\u62ec\u9905\u4e7e\u3001\u86cb\u7cd5\u3001\u725b\u89d2\u5305croissants\u3001\u66f2\u5947cookies\u3001\u751c\u5708\u5708doughnuts\u3001\u7f8e\u5f0f\u9b06\u9905muffins\u7b49)\u7b49\u3002\n\n\n\u4e8c\u3001\u88dc\u5145\u8aaa\u660e\n\u7d14\u7d20\u98f2\u98df\u88e1\u7684\u690d\u5316\u7d20\uff08Phytochemicals\uff09\uff0c\u690d\u5316\u7d20\u70ba\u690d\u7269\u7684\u514d\u75ab\u7cfb\u7d71\uff0c\u5b83\u662f\u690d\u7269\u751f\u9577\u7684\u5fc5\u8981\u5143\u7d20\uff0c\u4e5f\u662f\u690d\u7269\u4e94\u984f\u516d\u8272\u4e4b\u5929\u7136\u8272\u7d20\u548c\u690d\u7269\u6c23\u5473\u4e4b\u7269\u8cea\u4f86\u6e90\u3002\n\n\u690d\u5316\u7d20\u4f5c\u7528\uff1a\n\uff08\u4e00\uff09\u63d0\u4f9b\u690d\u7269\u81ea\u6211\u4fdd\u8b77\u7684\u529f\u80fd\uff0c\u62b5\u6297\u6606\u87f2\u3001\u7d30\u83cc\u3001\u771f\u83cc\u3001\u75c5\u6bd2\u7684\u611f\u67d3\u50b7\u5bb3\u3002\n\uff08\u4e8c\uff09\u5c0d\u7d2b\u5916\u7dda\uff0c\u8f3b\u5c04\u7dda\uff0c\u7a7a\u6c23\u53ca\u571f\u58e4\u6c61\u67d3\uff0c\u5316\u5b78\u85e5\u7269\u4e4b\u7a2e\u7a2e\u50b7\u5bb3\u4e4b\u4fdd\u8b77\u4f5c\u7528\u3002\n\n\u5c0d\u4eba\u985e\u800c\u8a00\uff0c\u690d\u5316\u7d20\u96d6\u5c6c\u300c\u975e\u5fc5\u8981\u6027\u71df\u990a\u7d20\u300d\u4f46\u56e0\u4eba\u9ad4\u672c\u8eab\u7121\u6cd5\u88fd\u9020\u690d\u5316\u7d20\uff0c\u5fc5\u9808\u5f9e\u5404\u7a2e\u98df\u7269\u4f86\u651d\u53d6\u9019\u4e9b\u6709\u76ca\u4eba\u9ad4\u5065\u5eb7\u7684\u71df\u990a\u6210\u5206\uff0c\u7d71\u7a31\u690d\u7269\u71df\u990a\u7d20\uff08phytonutrient\uff09\uff0c\u4ea6\u6709\u300c21\u4e16\u7d00\u7684\u7dad\u751f\u7d20\u300d\u4e4b\u7a31\u3002\n\n\u690d\u5316\u7d20\u5c0d\u4eba\u9ad4\u7684\u4f5c\u7528\uff0c\u5 Brustkrebs ist in Europa die unter Frauen meistverbreitete Krebsart. Sie tritt bei vielen in der Lebensphase auf, in der sie sich der Karriere und der Familie widmen. Obwohl Patientinnen ha\u0308ufig eine Chemotherapie empfohlen wird, konnten Studien zeigen, dass weniger als 10 % der Patientinnen mit Brustkrebs im Fru\u0308hstadium von einer Chemotherapie profitieren.\n\nDer Oncotype DX wurde entwickelt, um auf Grundlage von Informationen u\u0308ber die Biologie des individuellen Brustkrebses eine sinnvolle Therapieentscheidung zu treffen und die Behandlung individuell abzustimmen. Der Test verringert die Anzahl der unno\u0308tigen Chemotherapien und die damit einhergehenden Kosten fu\u0308r das Gesundheitswesen signifikant. Eine deutsche Analyse aus dem Jahr 2017 scha\u0308tzt die mo\u0308glichen Einsparungen bei den gesamtgesellschaftlichen Kosten durch den Test auf mehr als 253 Millionen Euro pro Jahr.\n\nOncotype DX ist in den wichtigsten internationalen Leitlinien enthalten und wird von verschiedenen Gesundheitssystemen in Europa erstattet. Nach Bewertung und Empfehlung durch das NICE im Jahr 2013 ist der Test fu\u0308r alle britischen Patientinnen mittlerweile sehr gut verfu\u0308gbar. Patientinnen in Frankreich ko\u0308nnen den Oncotype DX dank eines speziellen Finanzierungsmodells fu\u0308r innovative Diagnostik nutzen. In Europa erstatten u. a. die Schweiz, Irland, Griechenland und Spanien den Test.\n\n\u2014 \u2014 \u2014 \u2014 \u2014 \u2014 \n\u2014 \u2014 \u2014 \u2014 \u2014 \u2014 \n\nWeitere Informationen erh\u00e4ltst du:\n\u00dcber den Oncotype DX: www.oncotypeiq.de\nWeitere Artikel \u00fcber Brustkrebs: https://medizin-aspekte.de/?s=brustkrebs\n\n\u2014 \u2014 \u2014 \u2014 \u2014 \u2014 \n\u2014 \u2014 \u2014 \u2014 \u2014 \u2014 \n\n\u25ba Facebook: https://goo.gl/2SFUHw\n\u25ba YouTube: https://goo.gl/HgQTtf\n\u25ba Twitter: https://goo.gl/Gu3K6a\n\u25ba Website: https://goo.gl/MERqA4\n\n\u2014 \u2014 \u2014 \u2014 \u2014 \u2014 \n\u2014 \u2014 \u2014 \u2014 \u2014 \u2014\n\nQuellen / Publikationen:\n\nIKK BB - Innungskrankenkasse Brandenburg und Berlin (PM, 04.12.17)\n\nEUCAN. 2012. Key aspects of the LVE include: (1) it is open source and compatible with open source hardware and software, making it inexpensive and widely accessible to the 3D printing community, (2) it utilizes a standard 60 mL syringe as its ink reservoir, effectively increasing print volume of the average bioprinter, (3) it is capable of retraction and high speed movements, and (4) it can print fluids using nozzle diameters as small as 100 \u03bcm, enabling the printing of complex shapes/objects when used in conjunction with the freeform reversible embedding of suspended hydrogels (FRESH) 3D printing method.   \n\nComplete instructions for printing, building and using the LVE are available in the open-access publication in the Journal Hardware X at https://doi.org/10.1016/j.ohx.2018.02.001. Webb, M.D.", "publishedAt": "2019-10-28T22:00:10Z", "description": "In this video, Dr. Webb shows the 3D Biomechanical Gait Lab at Texas Back Institute in Plano, Texas and how it can help improve patient outcomes in Spine Surgery. \n\nWhat is the Spine Biomechanical Gait Lab?\nThe Spine Biomechanics Laboratory at Texas Back Institute Research Foundation works to investigate the biomechanical risk factors associated with spinal ailments in an effort to define the most appropriate and effective treatment options.\n\nThe laboratory is actively studying patients with scoliosis, cervical and thoracic myelopathy, chronic back and neck pain, sacroiliac joint dysfunction, and total disc replacement for lumbar and cervical degeneration. Within each group, the researchers are comparing gait, balance, lifting, sit-to-stand motion, and stair climbing before and after several types of treatments.\n\nThe biomechanical analysis can help determine if patients are using muscles efficiently after surgery and if their muscles are coordinated. The findings can be used to help fine tune physical therapy programs and help motivate patients to continue exercising. \n\nThe lab is the first spine-related human movement biomechanics lab to be incorporated within a private practice spine center in the United States. \n\nFor more info, you can visit: www.texasback.com\n\nYou can connect with Dr. Haddas at\nLinkedin: https://www.linkedin.com/in/rhaddas/\nResearch gate: https://www.researchgate.net/profile/Ram_Haddas\n\nHaddas R, Cox J, Belanger T, Boah AO, Ju KL, Derman PB. "Australian-German Climate & Energy College", "publishedAt": "2019-06-28T04:57:19Z", "description": "Sina Khatami, 26 June 2019.\n\nSina Khatami: On the topic of climate change, there are two camps of politicians absolving themselves from responsibility. Politicians who deny or cast scepticism about the anthropogenic nature of climate change and/or its substantial implications; and those who blame climate change for the detrimental environmental impacts of their policies.\n\nPosing the very question \u201cclimatic or regionally induced by humans?\u201d, we investigated the dramatic drying of Lake Urmia over the past decades. Lake Urmia\u2014a unique aquatic ecosystem and UNESCO designated Biosphere Reserve\u2014has shrunk by around 80% of its volume compared to 1970s. Lake Urmia drying is a quintessential example of environmental tragedies happening around the globe.\n\nAnalysing ground and satellite hydro-climatic data over the past five decades, we showed that the lake desiccation has been driven by aggressive and unsustainable expansion of agricultural activities and water withdrawals upstream, and that climatic factors have played only a small or negligible role so far. Chloe Moreau et al (2018), Current Biology https://doi.org/10.1016/j.cub.2018.11.009\n\nLimb position along the body is highly consistent within one species but very variable among vertebrates. Despite major advances in our understanding of limb patterning in three dimensions, how limbs reproducibly form along the antero-posterior axis remains largely unknown. Hox genes have long been suspected to control limb position; however, supporting evidences are mostly correlative and their role in this process is unclear.\n\nHere, we show that limb position is determined early in development through the action of Hox genes. Dynamic lineage analysis revealed that, during gastrulation, the forelimb, interlimb, and hindlimb fields are progressively generated and concomitantly patterned by the collinear activation of Hox genes in a two-step process.\n\nFirst, the sequential activation of Hoxb genes controls the relative position of their own collinear domains of expression in the forming lateral plate mesoderm, as demonstrated by functional perturbations during gastrulation. Then, within these collinear domains, we show that Hoxb4 anteriorly and Hox9 genes posteriorly, respectively, activate and repress the expression of the forelimb initiation gene Tbx5 and instruct the definitive position of the forelimb.\n\nFurthermore, by comparing the dynamics of Hoxb genes activation during zebra finch, chicken, and ostrich gastrulation, we provide evidences that changes in the timing of collinear Hox gene activation might underlie natural variation in forelimb position between different birds. Altogether, our results that characterize the cellular and molecular mechanisms underlying the regulation and natural variation of forelimb positioning in avians show a direct and early role for Hox genes in this process.\n\nGood channel: https://www.youtube.com/Dlium\nSubscribe, like and comment.\n\nGood website: https://www.dlium.com\nBookmark, subscribe and comment.", "tags": ["Current Biology", "limb", "lateral plate mesoderm", "gastrulation", "Hox genes", "Tbx5", "patterning", "chicken", "birds", "collinearity"], "title": "Timed Collinear Activation of Hox Genes during Gastrulation Controls the Avian Forelimb Position", "channelId": "UC32BboXfQ_tDCV8y1ttx7cg"}, "contentDetails": {"duration": "PT1M26S"}, "statistics": {"viewCount": "75", "dislikeCount": "0", "likeCount": "2", "favoriteCount": "0", "commentCount": "0"}, "id": "SFoHYGdUGco"}], "idx_paper": "10.1016/j.is.2018.11.009"}, {"q": "10.1016/j.is.2018.11.009", "items": [{"snippet": {"channelTitle": "Gerwin Wulf", "channelId": "UC_wDBHa7iggB1EiNeb7jfVQ", "publishedAt": "2018-11-14T16:37:43Z", "description": "Mars on Earth! This process involves external forces which may be dangerous, for example in an unmanned aerial vehicle (UAV) that interacts with unknown environment. There are numerous potential applications in UAVs that require physical interaction with its environment. However, this scenario brings evident challenges to be addressed, i.e., (i) the dedicated parts for the physical interaction (e.g., robotic arm) might change the moment of inertias and the center of gravity of the UAVs; (ii) contact phase might cause chattering effects; (iii) versatile external forces during interaction can degrade the performance; (iv) the needs of the UAVs to respect the bounds on the controller actions as well as the upper limits of the additional sensors equipped with a tool. In order to handle the aforementioned challenges in a systematic way, an optimization\u2013based approach is proposed for use on the control and the estimation design. The translational states and unmeasured forces are estimated by nonlinear moving horizon estimation (NMHE) after each new measurement becomes available. The estimated external forces are then fed into the nonlinear model predictive control (NMPC) which provides the total force and three angular positions. For the total forces, a novel control allocation is designed to maintain the interaction with the ceiling at the desired level. The angular values, three outputs of NMPC, are given to proportional\u2013derivative\u2013integral (PID) controllers to maintain attitude stability. Using the external force information given by the NMHE, the presented interaction controller is able to interact with the environment experimentally in milliseconds.\n\nNote: This link may provide free access to the full-text article until 12th of March 2019:  https://authors.elsevier.com/c/1YRGh3PiEzpypA", "tags": ["Science & Technology"], "title": "Model Predictive UAV-Tool Interaction Control Enhanced by External Forces", "channelId": "UC6P-B_4is8cIdFWEvFvpuPA"}, "contentDetails": {"duration": "PT1M45S"}, "statistics": {"viewCount": "360", "dislikeCount": "0", "likeCount": "3", "favoriteCount": "0", "commentCount": "0"}, "id": "MWuV5bkyQ0Q"}], "idx_paper": "10.1016/j.is.2019.01.004"}, {"q": "10.1016/j.is.2019.01.004", "items": [{"snippet": {"defaultAudioLanguage": "pt", "channelTitle": "Canal Comporta", "publishedAt": "2019-11-27T21:00:13Z", "description": "Hoje vamos falar da agressiva e assustadora aranha armadeira! Wernicke\u2019s encephalopathy is a triad of symptoms of confusion, internuclear ophthalmoplegia, and confabulation The treatment for Wernicke\u2019s is IV thiamine or vitamin B1 Untreated Wernicke\u2019s leads to Korsakoff's syndrome where a prolonged thiamine deficiency leads to worsening brain function  Subdural hematomas from torn bridging veins are common in alcoholics because of the combination of frequent falls and cerebral atrophy caused by alcohol. Diagnostic tests including culture and other mycological tests for mold pathogens have reduced sensitivities particularly in patients on mold-active antifungal prophylaxis. Performance of currently available tests and biomarkers for invasive mold infections may be enhanced by combination with sensitive and specific immunological markers. Martin Hoenigl, the current president of the European Confederation of Medical Mycology (ECMM) and Assistant Professor at the University of California, San Diego, discusses the potential of immunologic markers for diagnosis and treatment monitoring of invasive mold infections.\n\n\nDurch Schimmelpilze wie Aspergillus spp. ausgel\u00f6ste invasive Infektionen k\u00f6nnen schwierig zu diagnostizieren sein und sind gleichzeitig mit einer hohen Morbidit\u00e4t und Mortalit\u00e4t assoziiert. Kulturen oder andere mykologische Tests f\u00fcr Schimmelpilze haben insbesondere in Patienten, die eine Prophylaxe gegen Pilzerkrankungen erhalten, eine verringerte Sensitivit\u00e4t. Derzeit verf\u00fcgbare Tests und Biomarker f\u00fcr invasive Schimmelpilzerkrankungen k\u00f6nnen durch Kombination mit sensitiven und spezifischen immunologischen Markern verbessert werden. Martin Hoenigl, derzeitiger Pr\u00e4sident der European Confederation of Medical Mycology (ECMM) und Assistant Professor an der University of California, San Diego, referiert \u00fcber das Potential immunologischer Marker f\u00fcr Diagnose und Therapie\u00fcberwachung invasiver Pilzerkrankungen. \n\n\n\nRelated articles:\nhttps://doi.org/10.1111/myc.12679 \nhttps://doi.org/10.1016/j.jinf.2018.05.001 \nhttps://doi.org/10.3389/fimmu.2019.01798 \nhttps://doi.org/10.3390/jof5040116  \n\n\n\n---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\nMusic by Goldklang Production Studio (Nutzungsrecht einger\u00e4umt)\nVideo by Martin Hoenigl\nEditing by NCXT - Catherine E. Sheppard et al (2018), Current Biology https://doi.org/10.1016/j.cub.2018.05.001\n\nCultural inheritance, the transmission of socially learned information across generations, is a non-genetic, \u201csecond inheritance system\u201d capable of shaping phenotypic variation in humans and many non-human animals. Studies of wild animals show that conformity and biases toward copying particular individuals can result in the rapid spread of culturally transmitted behavioral traits and a consequent increase in behavioral homogeneity within groups and populations.\n\nThese findings support classic models of cultural evolution, which predict that many-to-one or one-to-many transmission erodes within-group variance in culturally inherited traits. However, classic theory also predicts that within-group heterogeneity is preserved when offspring each learn from an exclusive role model. We tested this prediction in a wild mammal, the banded mongoose (Mungos mungo), in which offspring are reared by specific adult carers that are not their parents, providing an opportunity to disentangle genetic and cultural inheritance of behavior.\n\nWe show using stable isotope analysis that young mongooses inherit their adult foraging niche from cultural role models, not from their genetic parents. As predicted by theory, one-to-one cultural transmission prevented blending inheritance and allowed the stable coexistence of distinct behavioral traditions within the same social groups. Our results confirm that cultural inheritance via role models can promote rather than erode behavioral heterogeneity in natural populations.\n\nGood channel: https://www.youtube.com/Dlium\nSubscribe, like and comment.\n\nGood website: https://www.dlium.com\nBookmark, subscribe and comment.", "tags": ["Current Biology", "Mungos mungo"], "title": "Decoupling of Genetic and Cultural Inheritance in a Wild Mammal", "channelId": "UC32BboXfQ_tDCV8y1ttx7cg"}, "contentDetails": {"duration": "PT42S"}, "statistics": {"viewCount": "26", "dislikeCount": "0", "likeCount": "1", "favoriteCount": "0", "commentCount": "1"}, "id": "A2dAFERatl8"}], "idx_paper": "10.1016/j.im.2018.05.001"}, {"q": "10.1016/j.im.2018.05.001", "items": [{"snippet": {"defaultAudioLanguage": "en", "channelTitle": "Curepoint Acupuncture", "publishedAt": "2020-02-02T19:10:08Z", "description": "This video explains how acupuncture works in general. Stem cells also provide the resources that different organs and tissues need to repair themselves after any damage or injury. Certain types of adult stem cells are even used in the laboratory for treatment of a range of diseases related to cells or tissues.\n\nWhat Happens as We Age?\nAs we age, our stem cells slow down, in terms of their productivity and regeneration rate, for several reasons . Thus, with time, their ability to function within our body declines. Cells in the body\u2019s tissues, particularly intestinal tissues, blood, and the nervous system become less functional and, in some cases, alter their functions as well. Consequently, the regeneration of new intestinal cells also falters. This process poses a threat to our gastrointestinal system as any infection, injury, or other diseases will be able to last longer, and our ability to fight it will be weaker.\n\nHow Does Fasting Help with Stem Cell Regeneration?\n\nSurprisingly, fasting can help with stem cell regeneration. While looking into this phenomenon, MIT biologists, Prof. Omer Yilmaz, and Prof. David Sabatini found out that the aging of stem cells could be reversed through fasting . To put this theory to the test, the biologists tested the effects of fasting on laboratory mice of different ages. They observed how the regeneration process of stem cells reacted to food deprivation during a 24-hour fast. Retrieved from https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=OZhzaG5OHE4\n\nFind more info about my research here:\n\nhttps://www.growkudos.com/profiles/22963\nhttps://www.researchgate.net/profile/Sergio_Torres-Martinez\nhttps://publons.com/author/1414281/sergio-torres-martinez\nhttp://orcid.org/0000-0002-8823-1676\nhttp://www.researcherid.com/rid/D-1461-2016\n@RESSTOOLBOX\n\nMusic: https://www.bensound.com\n\nExploring attachment patterns between multi-word\nverbs and argument structure constructions\nSergio Torres-Mart\u00ednez *\nUniversidad de Antioquia, Medell\u00edn, Colombia\nReceived 14 November2017; received in revised form 15 February 2018; accepted 2 April 2018\nhttps://doi.org/10.1016/j.lingua.2018.04.001\n\nAbstract\nThe present paper reports the results of two corpus studies of multi-word verbs in the context of Cognitive Construction Grammar.  The main claim of the constructionist approach adopted in this paper is that the meaning of specific multi-word verbs (MWVs), that is, combinations of a verb proper and a particle (spatial adverb, preposition, or both), overlaps the meaning of the argument structure construction in which it appears, thereby facilitating the positing of motivated categories. This theoretical claim is supported by the results of a two-staged corpus study. The first part of the study uses the affordances of the online interface of the 520-million-word Corpus of Contemporary American English (COCA). The results show that the identified MWVs in the corpus are skewed toward motional usages in spoken registers. The list of frequent MWVs provides the data for the second study. In this case, the results confirm the hypothesis that MWVs overlap specific argument structure constructions following distinct attachment patterns. This finding also suggests that argument structure constructions are high-order constructions that interface thought and language at a deep cognitive level.\n\nKeywords:\nArgument Structure Constructions; MWV-ASC attachment patterns; Cognitive Construction Grammar; constructions; embodiment; motivation; multi-word verbs\n\nREFERENCES\n\nHaugeland, J. This process involves external forces which may be dangerous, for example in an unmanned aerial vehicle (UAV) that interacts with unknown environment. There are numerous potential applications in UAVs that require physical interaction with its environment. However, this scenario brings evident challenges to be addressed, i.e., (i) the dedicated parts for the physical interaction (e.g., robotic arm) might change the moment of inertias and the center of gravity of the UAVs; (ii) contact phase might cause chattering effects; (iii) versatile external forces during interaction can degrade the performance; (iv) the needs of the UAVs to respect the bounds on the controller actions as well as the upper limits of the additional sensors equipped with a tool. In order to handle the aforementioned challenges in a systematic way, an optimization\u2013based approach is proposed for use on the control and the estimation design. The translational states and unmeasured forces are estimated by nonlinear moving horizon estimation (NMHE) after each new measurement becomes available. The estimated external forces are then fed into the nonlinear model predictive control (NMPC) which provides the total force and three angular positions. For the total forces, a novel control allocation is designed to maintain the interaction with the ceiling at the desired level. The angular values, three outputs of NMPC, are given to proportional\u2013derivative\u2013integral (PID) controllers to maintain attitude stability. Using the external force information given by the NMHE, the presented interaction controller is able to interact with the environment experimentally in milliseconds.\n\nNote: This link may provide free access to the full-text article until 12th of March 2019:  https://authors.elsevier.com/c/1YRGh3PiEzpypA", "tags": ["Science & Technology"], "title": "Model Predictive UAV-Tool Interaction Control Enhanced by External Forces", "channelId": "UC6P-B_4is8cIdFWEvFvpuPA"}, "contentDetails": {"duration": "PT1M45S"}, "statistics": {"viewCount": "360", "dislikeCount": "0", "likeCount": "3", "favoriteCount": "0", "commentCount": "0"}, "id": "MWuV5bkyQ0Q"}], "idx_paper": "10.1016/j.robot.2019.01.004"}, {"q": "10.1016/j.robot.2018.12.003", "items": [{"snippet": {"channelTitle": "Gilbert Wang", "channelId": "UCwVZzjwdwHX7ajq9gcqmB4g", "publishedAt": "2019-03-03T05:36:26Z", "description": "The triangular soft rolling robot is constructed by mounting three CPAM soft actuators on one side of a transparent PVC membrane and then folding the membrane into a triangular prism with the CPAM-mounted surface as the inner surface. The redundancy is often generated for the purpose of resolving the time constraint of fast-activating pathways. \n\n\n\nLarge numbers should not be considered wasteful, but are necessary for generating the fastest possible response and make possible rare events that otherwise would never happen. This property is universal, ranging from the molecular scale to the population level. \n\n\n\nD. Holcman\n\n\n[1] Schuss, Z., Basnayake, K., & Holcman, D. (2019).
